Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mule
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mule according to what we have said about the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit at all, then there are three manners of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Here is the translation:
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After I place the two puffed-up nerves so that the key is perceived from the other side, and then remove the fire cautery, thus there will be four. If you see, then cauterize the entire cautery to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has brought forth purulence by long time, and this is worth more than the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery does not work on a dropsical person, except by the method which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the mouth, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the kidneys, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the breast; and let the cauterizations be well near the spot where the key fits.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery open to let it heal for a long time, and do not cease the care of the patient after the cautery; and salvation will hasten, and there will be together the two intentions with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the same as the one we have shown before, and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what was said earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen to one who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish pus, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and index finger; and lift up your hand with the cautery as if turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far in, thus the yellowish pus would burst forth, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make two cauteries on each leg, one at the tip of the little toe and one behind the knee, on the inside of the leg; and let the cauteries be long, one under the kneecap in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time until the moisture subsides; after cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by any methods; and you see the patient suffering badly and with great virtue, if make one great cautery on the stomach according to what is spoken here before or the cautery of the stomach, to the circulatory cautery; and three subtle cauterizations around the mouth, each a small, subtle cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each toe, and two small cauterizations on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the ulcers are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and made of thick, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that one which is entirely below the almond-shaped prominence and pokes and pokes in a triangular way, and one cauterization under the jawbone, two fingers' breadth; and if you think that his stomach has grown cold, and the food does not cook, and the face begins to puff up, then on the face make a large cauterization on the stomach, as is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the belly at all the cauterized part; and leave the cauterizer open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure let the limb remain until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, if it seems like a razor, then put the cautery all ablaze on that thelul cut; and I leave it for as long as the cauterizations come to the beginning of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after that, cure with ointments that are beneficial until they are sound; and if you make a great cautery on the alchatim, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure surgery or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes such a disease that it cannot be healed unless by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When an abscess forms and is swollen and discharges pus and corrupt moistrures, then you must examine the entire tent and know exactly how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After reheat the cautery that seems razor-sharp, and insert it into the abscess according to the amount that the tent has entered, and continue the cautery until all corrupt flesh is burned away, once, twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of what needs to be done; and beware of burning the nerve that is nearby, and from great wounds.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the abscess goes to the bladder and intestine, then beware of these places, and do not make any fires except on solid ground, and think that they are not yet passed through; after the cure let the limb remain until it is healed, and if the swelling subsides and the materials have been removed for a long time, then know that the swelling is entirely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the swelling is torn, and corrupts the bone at its root; and thus as one of those things which we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take a feminine shape, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other at the subtle cautery that we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will bring greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part in front of the bladder, where the hair of the wrist begins, and one to the right and one to the left, and each of them be as long as the length of a finger; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauterizations be subtle according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their terminations are late; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that three cauterizations be made around the mouth, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be subtle, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip of the hainche, and because of this the patient's limb is moved from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the patient has a departure in the region of the hips, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip of the hainche with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the limb around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations on the olive, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the veins; and cure until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip of the hainche, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division, but the cure does not hold, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you cauterize above the buttock bone three triangular cauteries in this shape, and make good depth and great, and have between each cautery the width of an elbow, and be the cauteries oval; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle above the chief of the buttock bone, why there are four according to this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cautery of the circle that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all the hip and all the tendons of the knee are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the buttock and does not reach as far as the thigh nor as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then you make two cauteries on either side where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingerbreadths to the left; and be the cauteries cutellate, and let the burning be done in the thickness of the skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the toes or almost there, then you cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary is, make him have more; and if it seems that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the cutaneous or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cauterization until you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they were left so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a fire cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say about the fire cautery of the flank, how it is done, make such a rod and be as wide as an egg of dactyl or a little less, and be between the ribs and be from one rib to another in the quantity of a walnut; and be the ribs apart two parts, and also like hazelnuts, and it must be well made with iron; and that is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et soit eschaufez tant qu'il soit toz rouges et giete senteles,
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this fire cautery because of the fear of its regard, and if we see few who use it; and nonetheless, it is one of the good cauteries that can suffer it, and the place where it afflicts.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning cauteries of medicine are such that you make an instrument with notches in which the edges descend below the door frame, and it is made of earth or iron to a length of one palm, and on the top have two noses, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a dove; and they be open at the front and back, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put the pommel of the haunch on the patient lying on his healthy side, and then place your hand right over the pommel of the haunch; after that pour hot water between the two circles of the awn which is heated by fire one pot, and let it stay for an hour or a tenth, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning of him.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a similar mordication as fire; and when the mordications are passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the haunch of sweet water, and let it stay thus three days, and put on butter until what is black from scabbing is removed; and after three days that putrefaction ceases; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments as long as he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make an instrument that holds heat according to what you have done in a similar way in the groin; and this is the method of hot treatment, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and live heat, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	or there is a small hole to drain what the point of a razor can enter; and put it into another pot well weighted, and put sweet heat on top, as long as there are two powders above which you will have well prepared in your hand; and leave it thus until the heat descends and becomes water or fluid in the weighed pot, then take all that heat and pour it on charcoal and alkaline just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very helpful and administered in the movements of medical works and in other members' cauterizations. For it performs a work like fire, and also with other medicines that one well cures the flesh thus as thesis and honeyed anacardium and chalices with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us about a cure where one man was cured of the pain in his flesh and sciatic vein, and greatly praised it, and said that no other cure was done to him, and he was healed only once when this cure was performed, and he bathed himself just as it is instructed here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same way that you take green litargire and make it very fine with a little bit of grease, and put it on the flesh, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it there for three hours and by the quantity that the patient does not feel the heat anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cauterization of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fire, it helps a lot; and one should make the cauterizations in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take flax and soak it in old oil, and place it on the fossa that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called fascia.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that take goat's fire when it is dry, and put it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the flax, and let it stay until it cools down; and do it again like this, and don't stop doing it like this as long as you think with your senses that it will reach the hunch and that the pain will cease; and this manner of cauterization is called "goat's fire".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or striking or from too great evacuation or from similar things spread cold matter, none of these similarities is worth cauterizing except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient be freed from fetid pills or other similar things, and one should place them on their back, where the pain stays, three lines marked with a cross, and in each line .v. cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and the cauterization should be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make iij. cauterizations or iiij. at the clavicle median according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow back when they wake up, and fear; and you will find in the last part of the spine of the back and in no other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it curing, then cauterize it at the cautery of celery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery reaches every part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the fire that is piercing 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, leave it so long as it is sound according to what we have said, and take care not to apply cauterization in a hollow spot where there is a swelling of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain in the joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the barber calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make many cauteries around the jointure of the foot, and be the cauteries olive-like according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make the cauterization all over with the fire that we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make cauterization on each knee 3 or 4 times for every part, all over the olivary; and if you need more, do it more, but do not keep your hand there any longer than until the fat of the cheek is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then make punctures around the joint for two lines; and if there remains no pain to the arm, then make punctures above each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the shoulders or as far as the sides, then cauterize each part, and perform good governance with the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you provide good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the scab
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When scurvy comes in sores, and the boils descend to the groin and it's new, then it is necessary that when you see it curing, that he does not move at all on that day; and that he uses things which loosen his bowels, so that the phlegm descends from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his backbone until the boil is repaired, and bring them down to your knees, and mark an incision below the scurvy on the bone of the thumb, and at all a sign that is similar to the middle of a circle above the body; then cauterize it according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is pale and emits sweat.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reposition the bones to their place; and hold his hand firmly so that he does not return to that place; and work well on the patient's hips, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the hips, and another under the breast holding his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again as many times as necessary until you reach the bone; and be careful subtly so that the bones do not shift when you do the cautery; lest you burn him; and lest the patient die or receive other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the fire cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their size, and those of great people also great according to their size; after three days, care for the wound at the site of the burning until the scabbing is removed; afterwards, care for other ointments until they are healed, and the patient lies on his back for 40 days with a cushion so that the wound may be well closed; and it is necessary that their bandages be worn long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he will go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, let a well-made bandage be given to him, and wear it for another 40 days; and may he have good rest, so that he does not trouble himself too much and take care not to eat or drink too much and shout too loudly; and when he has done this instruction, then he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter about the cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the scurvy of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, then one should make the fire cautery of the fire again according to its quantity, and let it be burned the third time by the cure; after the cure according to what we have said; and any of the ancients have said that one must cauterize at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of entrance and make a line above the ulcer for its width, and another below it, and with your hand guide all the cautery through.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more tender.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pains in any member.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauterization be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location of twistings and pains.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, that's well; if not, begin another cauterization on that one, for such a habit is that it must change to the member that is closest, therefore you should make cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	surgeonry
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are helped sometimes by cauterization with great help, and similarly the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see it being cauterized, take care if the sickness is at its beginning, and if it's cured according to what we said in the division, and don't let it spread or remain, and you doubt that corruption will overwhelm the whole patient, then make V cauterizations on the head: I in the middle of the head about nine inches, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on the two horns, and I behind on the hinder part; and leave your hand there until the cautery comes to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can come out; and cauterize on the mole according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgeonship is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries on the head, and one cautery in the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back, and one great one on the scapula and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I do of cauterization, the more it helps and produces profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization as much as the healthy person feels, because the body is already too corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward, dress with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and he is not yet healed, then make a cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be slightly entering into the flesh of the skin; then cure it with ointments until he is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one makes a fire cautery on the arm and foot and back at the end of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and yet no one intervenes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and exits of nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is worth nothing, then cauterize it with one cautery a little deep, according to the thickness of the flesh of the knee, until the pus is removed, and its color is changed; then cure with flour of vetches and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of calf and blood of almond, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of chancres by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning and you wish to arrest it, then cauterize around the perimeter of the circle with the fire that seems like a ring, entirely around the tour of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; and yet it does not seem to me good, for I fear that it would be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen sometimes; and it is a more direct thing that it be cauterized around, with the fire called "circule", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays death or due to the superfluity that it causes or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or due to the weather; and you see it hastening towards death: then cauterize it with many small cauterizations while it pricks; afterwards leave it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten its dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery so that its form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauterizations have pierced the furrow, and be such cauterizations that the patient feels them outside in just such a way that the flow of pus is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterward care for it until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the member, for it consumes the members just as fire dries out dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in the place that can suffer a fire cautery together, then sharpen the cauters little and great, according to what is needed for the place where the illness is; after cauterizing all parts until you root out all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupt be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice that suffers with oil until the burn marks of fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments generates flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not arise, it is good; and if not, then restart the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has been sometimes used in place of fire cauterization by medicinal treatment; but nevertheless fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said the cure by medicinal treatment in the division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Mout de fois avient que as piez par defours naist une maladie qui est apelee "clos" selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose faultree qui blece le pied.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to know fire cauterization and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is when you heat the cautery iron like a blacksmith's pen, and make it of good steel to its measure so that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and have subtle edges; then put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it reaches the root of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to suppurate; then apply a poultice made of wild marjoram bruised with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with ointment, anointing it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by external wounds to the body, and many times occur on hands and feet, then it is necessary that you apply water cauterization; and do so: take a linen cord or iron, or a quill of vetch, and place it on the claw and nail, that is, pimpled veins; and place the cord around so that it envelops everything completely, then put in a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the cord comes to the root of the claw, and thus the hot water can find its way deep to the root; and allow the patient a little time for the burning of the hot water one hour; then leave it like this, and he will come loose from all his roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So that you can do one after another, as long as you have reached all those who are in the body, then cure the wounds which cause flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from coldness or numbness, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make .iiii. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the weight, and one on the stomach at the olivaire cautery; if the trembling ceases, and the health of the cold disease hastens.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No time appears by foreknowledge to know when the cleansed body, or foul boils, that come from corrupted great matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary at first when they appear to make a fire cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization made from myrtle wood, by which the point is seized by fire, or from a long aristologe root, or a lentil-shaped cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And no time should cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further ahead, but the superfluous parts that come from it are broken off, and they heal; but it is necessary for this to be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at a cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is stilled under your fingers, and no more flows; then apply fire to the olivaire cauteries, many small and large ones, until they are all red; then take one, whether great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and put it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stemmed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to apply these one after another until the blood is stemmed; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well stem it, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stem blood; and let it be bound and restrained in a good manner.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever attempts to stem the bleeding by binding tightly with cloths or applying hot things on top, or other similar things, if it does not help at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press tightly until it is stemmed above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often while it is very cold, so that the blood may congeal and thicken and be stemmed; and make a way forward for those things which he needs, such as cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical cures
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the causes and symptoms and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter on the head until the end, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way for those things which one wishes to find more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to exercise greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come into cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who are so afflicted with their disease that they will die quickly due to the severity of their illness and the greatness of their malice; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these is one who gives you his sense, and says: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of and can take and hold; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your patients for the sake of their salvation; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and a memorial of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear friend, May Our Lord give you good understanding and rightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy breath of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ended this chapter by describing it in chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have described from head to foot, so that you may find more easily those things which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of pure water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often befalls children at birth, and when the midwife holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those that I have seen died suddenly; and for this reason it seems to me that it is not worth bothering with such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew thicker every day until it could not be sustained; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the operations are such that if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you cut a wide incision in the head; and make it as long as two nails, so that the moisture runs; and look here at the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more thickened and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opened up on each part, and the liquid jumps forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not respond to you: then you must make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all moisture forth.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After closing the cuts of cloths and powders, and putting in wine and oil, and leaving thus until the fifth day; then untie it, and treat the wound with tenting and anointings, and let the head drain equally, and then let the patient eat dry meat without moisture as long as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look at or open the great extent of the abscess, and the gathering of the liquid; for sometimes it is before; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the spot where the abscess opens and the liquid accumulates, and let the liquid flow according to what you have the power; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and come forth blood, so that the patient may die from the deprivation of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of rheum.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease which is called "catarre" in the eyes or at the liver, and the disease is old-fashioned, and the treatment of medicine does not help at all, then the final cure is the fire cauterization with what will be cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cover the views, it is necessary for the patient to make their head go back; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient remove their neck from the entire cloth; then look where the vein bites, and the pulsations of one and the other are after the ears, and they are then repointed; then mark the pulse on the inside, then cut off both with a sharp instrument, two parts deep, until the knife comes to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two should pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will jump out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space between III fingers, then sign and fill up just to the bone; and what needs to be done with blood is VI c/, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the sphac, cut so that apostemes do not come there, then bind the wound and tie, and the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migraine.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes and sharp catarra, due to the moistors of tears and heats in temples and old foreskin and similar things, and medicine does not help him by ways of medical treatments and all this does not profit him at all, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient bends back his hair from his temples, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little responded forth except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responded, then has the patient hold out his neck with some cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the liquid hot until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which is of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then train it upwards at the pincers, and depart well from the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the uncin, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if she is not cut open, then the blood will not flow entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And extract the blood of six cells up to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two knots of a strong double silk thread, so that no pus may come forth before the wound has healed and there may be bleeding; then cut off the superfluous part which is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize with the cutaneous cautery up to the bone as far as the hairs are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterization is aid to finish the moisture: therefore it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on well-made tents; and when one unties them, one must be careful with dry medicines that bring forth flesh, and with tents, until he is healed; and if there is no gap in the artery as long as you are working, then hasten to cauterize by fire, or apply the place with vitriol and strain it with your hand until the blood is stopped; and if you do not have that present, then put your finger on the place so that the blood may congeal, and raise the place with cold water so that the bleeding ceases, and be strained as needed; and what is more main and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire-cutting knife, but the cutting parts should be well spaced to withstand their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cutting parts are too close together, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have one big gap between the two cutlery, and then when you have marked with ink the two places, and you apply the hot iron on top so that it reaches up to the bone, and cut off the vein in two places; and let them be distant from each other between the two cells, for it is not sealed by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead of the chief part of the face, and it does not profit at all from the medicine one makes there, and you see the patient's face redness, and feel the forehead sensation as if from trembling; and thus oil are tense and moist so that the hairs of the papier are fallen, and the papier are heated and scalded by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to perform this cure.
