Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the "blunt cure" in olden times; and this is what you do to the patient with this disease: make them have hair on their forehead, then make three incisions on their forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions should be as big as two fingers inside the forehead going downwards to the nose, and the others two between the eyebrows above the papillae, and take care not to cut into the arteries that are between the eyebrows above the papillae; and keep your hand away from the continuity of the two jawbones, and make each wound three fingerbreadths across; and have a piece of sponge and many cloths ready in case the blood flows, then apply the poultice in three parts according to its shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is below the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the fat that is between the two cuts right down to the suture that is on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first cut the instrument called "culterelle", and it is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is soft, not at all sharp, and that's its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge of the scalpel towards the fatty part under the hide, and the edge softened towards the bone, and press until it reaches the main incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears under the hide; and then do the same in the main incision up to the other side; and then draw out equal blood, and express the place where the blood has been taken; then put a cloth of old cotton into each incision, and put damp cloths on it soaked in vinegar, oil, and ashes, and guard that abscesses do not form there; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great quantities of lukewarm water, then apply balm of basil with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with a great and accustomed cataract, and you see the eyes small and tight, and dimming the sight, and the pupils burned; and the hair is falling out, and there is a severe pain in the forehead, and the patient is strangled; then knows by these accidents that those matters and this cataract come from many veins, and the father of medicine who knows it, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to go back his forehead, then make a great cut in the middle of the forehead, and another one about a span wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision just up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood with a sponge, then place between the two lips of the incision a piece of old cotton and linen; then put wet cloths on it soaked in wine and oil, and take care to prevent hot abscesses; when it is cleansed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with caustic things that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of galenicals, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of three things: or grains, or beasts, or pebbles of stone, or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as ashes, vetches, peas; or flowing things, such as water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it gets into the ear or in any other way that does not join with the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill some violet oil or sesame oil, and then apply extraction; and when the procedure is finished, and the nostrils are stopped when the extraction comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and lift the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times a boil comes forth through this cure; and if it does not come forth, apply extraction with fine forceps, by which the shape is thus formed.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out through the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer an extraction with fine forceps of small double-jawed type; and if it doesn't come out through that, then make a chain of iron and insert the head of the chain or piercing of the ear very tightly, and stop whatever is around the chain from entering with wax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then treat it firmly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this way, take a glue from which birds take their nests, and put into some instrument that is pointed for that purpose, and wrap a little cotton around; then press the glue on the pebble or whatever it is, and treat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut open the ear before an abscess forms and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient's head bleed, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty part or dependent part; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the pebble, then remove it as much as you can, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains that are inside and they're inflamed, then administer an extraction; and if it can't come out, then administer one sharp spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do that when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then draw it out with fine forceps and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then that flows in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use an astringent condiment first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be fixed on that very ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps away because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many stones according to the length of the thread that you must hold taut and light, and heat them slightly over the fire; and put one or two perforations in the patient's ear, and raise it up with both feet from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to make this stone upon stone until the water comes out completely, and thus it jumps out completely; and if you see, then take a reed, and insert one of the heads into the ear, and the other head heats it over fire so long as the thickest part of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until the water comes out completely, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small in body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then administer an extraction with fine tweezers; and that's the easier thing to remove what's in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun: if there appear any worms, then treat them with subtle tweezers; and if none appear, take a string whose form this is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And bind the most subtle thread on the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then tie it firmly to the entire cord; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then wrap the cord with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations such as the ancients have experimented with in the elimination of worms, and you will find it or read about treating distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, because that is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is of silver or tin, narrow below to a small hole, and wide above to distill; and for pressing within the distillation with one instrument of well-made bronze for this purpose, and if you see, take one scraper and wrap around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into it, and all that you have of medicines on the string, and the string be in the ear; then push inside the scraper to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled out of the ear; and if the patient feels inside, and the distillation is a pot heated over fire so it distills into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a small hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through stopping of wounds or new growth inside the ear, and these stoppings often come very far into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there is one pot overflowing with the hole, and one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then the one that comes very far in, if one cannot see it, is from grievous cleansing in multiple dispositions, and in that which one can see, it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacity apparent, then work with all this spatula whose form this is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be gentle and careful in front of and behind all the way, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the opacity is from new growth or flesh of the ear, then hold it with subtle tweezers and cut lightly, until all that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the poultices are worn out in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it slightly by the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the popping sensation that patients complain of when they hear it, pierce lightly, and take care not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a poultice according to the width of the perforation, and moisten with Egyptian mummy.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on vitriol broth; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes from the decoration, then plunge a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paperwax.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This wax that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to spread with forceps and tweezers, and cut with a spatula of its roots; then put on the glass vitriol broth.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the wax peels off, then cauterize with a lenticular subtile cautery, and after the incision move slowly; and many times repair, until nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hellebore.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper the eyes one thing that seems like gruel in its form and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture on both sides of the paper above and below; the works are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the donation wide, then flay each part lightly, then take out with forceps.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot take it out without piercing the paper slightly, then do not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, tie it with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do nothing violent, for the ointments restore the flesh soon.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over and take the grandine with tweezers, cut and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the grandine is cut, let a solution of salt water flow, and cure the wound of those who bring forth flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is smeared on paper towels above, and this happens more to children than to grown-ups, and it troubles them greatly, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie down on their faces again, and sleep on top, and are their paper towels moist below their eyebrows covered by the swelling and appearance of exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lid onto your breasts and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient places their head in your lap; and then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then put it on them; and press with your fingers from one side to the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make a mixture of rose water and spatula, cutting a slit of the large size, but not greater than the wound or making a wound of vinegar; and make the skin smooth in depth until you reach the exinach; and in multiple dispositions, exinach comes from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Here is the translation:
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the surgeon does not open in the beginning of the cut, so slightly enlarge the cut until he sees; then pull it as we have said, then damp cloths in air and water, and put on the bandage, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who burn sulfur and put it on top in order to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is cleansed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes to a boil, then apply poultices soothingly until it is cleansed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs from paper grow differently than those of nature, and are whitened, they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of diseases as usual tears and softening of the papers and blurring, to the point of destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to four manners: either by fire cautery together, or by aqueous medicine as described in the chapter on cautery, and is made either by incision and suturing or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head on your shoulder, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, that's good; if not, put an awl through each thread above; and let this be at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow below these hairs, and draw one thread above all the paper, and turn it to a razor; then make in the part beneath the paper, beneath the hairs that are grown together, from the great tear to the small one; then pull out one thread, and put beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of an oak leaf, as the sprig of myrtle, and although it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the paper being divided into.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is someone who needs it, take a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then fill the spatula on both lines that you have signed, and begin from the large tear just a little bit; and be one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the thread into one of the two angles of the key, then scrape it all; then assemble the two lips with a seam of a needle to all the fine wool yarn, and wipe away the blood, and make the surplus threads on both sides to all things sticking, if you see fit to do so; and if not, then don't bother, just leave the seam and the threads for three or four days; then care for the wound without sewing anything constraining, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is muddy (as the ancients said), and that's a work without fear; and if there is another way: it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, to three separate threads according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what rises above the small forces equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and things are not equal, then take a needle where there is thread, and put it in the figure; and put one thread near the great drain, and the other thread near the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your two hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar assuaging ointments; and sometimes happen that the hairs of the paper are converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said about incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you transform the paper and make a hole within according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the surface are; and cut off at both ends of both parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what rises from the paper from the oil, and strain the two cauterizations from both parties together; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die, dry up, and fall away, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the wound has some forces, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and the hairs can no longer be felt; and this is the shape of the two hounds that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put one thread of soft and subtle silk on it; then assemble the threads and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then arrange in the chase another thread of fine silk briefly, and knot the end of the thread; then place the patient's head on your shoulder; and let it be under the sun so that the work is revealed, for this is a subtle and minute work; then put the needle through all the chase in the root of the hair grown together, and make it pierce the paper quickly as you guide it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it comes to the end of the chase on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the chase from below all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes forth from above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh is restored on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of the natural eyebrows, and raise it with that which you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pouring of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" comes to the eye, so there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or by incision, or by burning, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treatment is that you cut open this wound, and separate the lips of it, and put a linen cloth inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, then the disease returns worse than the first one; but it works with soft things, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or althea and flaxseed cooked, and oil of yarrow melted in some of the oils, and wrap a cloth around it, and cure it this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in the same form as it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing but remedies for this disease, so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is below which is truly called "axacrati" and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and tearing and cautery and similar things; and the way of working with it is that you take an awl which has a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce through the left forearm as far as the right side, so that the threads come out in two pieces of skin; then cut the flesh above all the awl, and the incision should be wide enough for a spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure on the paper comes out as it should, that's good; if not, then take a rasp and place it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuts inside the paper; and be the holes of the two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has no "I greece"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are grown below, from what follows the paper; then join the two severed parts with a thread of linen; then apply the cure for what we have said regarding soft medicines and poultices, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or an opening or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a linen cloth, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an engine to do everything they can to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling has occurred in the same way as the paper above is bound with white of oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary that you insert the point of a rasp under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers until you cut what is suitable for a subtle spatula, which is not too tight nor too loose, so that the patient cannot bear having the spatula too tight or causing harm to the oil; and make your incision, from which you remove this assembled part, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and let all this assembled part be healed, and sometimes in the oil add a little salty water, and lift up sweet water and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and place wet wool on top of it in abundance of eggs; and after three days use the colic remedy and similar things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the grime of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the grime is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moisture frozen, which when touched with iron and cooked between pincers, one cannot bear; and both forms begin near the large vein, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coils the grime between pincers with small double loops, and stretches it above; then take a needle, and insert one hair from a horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little bit and push it into the grime, and make it pierce all the way to the end of the needle, and tie the grime with a thread and stretch it above, and scrape off the rest on the side of the grime that follows the prune and silk until the hair reaches the head; then cut the remaining part in the root of the vein to all the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh or vein as it was before incision, so that through the incision the body does not produce tears habitually; and sometimes stretch the grime only to the onyx and thread, as we have said; then scrape off everything at the soft spatula of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision, throw a little bit of broom seed into the oil and a colic remedy made from litargyris, and leave it until the next day; then apply the treatment as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the grime is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the onyx cannot enter, many times this appearance of grime is treated with medicines; and it is born as I have told in the division, and when you see it growing, work the oil of the patient, and take a spatula slightly rough according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the grime above gently, and if you see that it is not diminishing and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the oil a colic remedy made from litargyris and red colic and broom seed, and stop the oil until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the oil, like an aposteme grows warm, then milk it, and first cure the warm aposteme until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh at the vein causes great harm in the oil, then suspend it to the onyx, and cut off a part and not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the oil a red colic remedy made from litargyris.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Es are some men's eyes that never have redness, and cover the prune-like skin and restrain on the papers and turn to the opposite direction, and seem like a rose of balustrade; and the work is such that the patient puts his head in one's hand, then opens the eyes, and keeps all the flesh fitting to this, and sustains with force; then cuts the first layer, and goes all cutting until the end, and takes care not to hurt the eye during the operation; and the incision should be as we have said in the incision of the tongue and with small forces, so that one removes the scab, just as the form shows after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all flesh removed, then drips oil from a seal or distills red liquid and similar corrosive medicines, and puts on the oil afterwards cotton with egg white, so that it becomes sure of hot aposteme; and if there remains nothing, and the wound starts to swell, and you doubt hot aposteme, then leave the oil and treat hot aposteme with soothing things for hot aposteme; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do all the flesh that has been removed from the eye by this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you hasten the cure of each weak eye by natural means; and by accidental means, in iron work; and do not put your hand on any of these operations until you see that this member is suffering from this operation.
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If veins are red that are covered on the eye, and tolerate the work of sight and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary then that you first look at the eye where the redness is, if it is elsewhere, and there is no other disease except for this redness; then take the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins all around according to your wisdom, and be the needles subtle double according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two ligatures by degree in one piece according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the forces those veins subtly, and remove the blood hour after hour, until you see removing those veins from the eye; and take care not to bleed the eye at all points of the scalp, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut off more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red pepper juice into the eye to corrupt what remains of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of that in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyelids, and let it be some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured of warm aposteme, then resume according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the abscess of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon so calls "arissati" abscess: when you cure it by cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in it that you cut into the aposteme, where it should decay, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then replace it with all the instruments that are there according to this form; and it is called "aspre chief", and make it from iron into one chief bent, and be pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some times, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the lump is congealed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowels is congealed, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not renew itself and is not apostemed, and bad things do not happen to it, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other cause than to bring the fistula back to the pertus of the navel according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone the second time with iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take a forest according to this form, and be the head of iron at three angles, and the fistula should be thinned out up to the chief as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier,
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyelids open fully and it does not come out of the neck or decrease, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal him, then put poultices or bandages made from iron to suck up, then put a lien on the eye made from aloes, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and drapes; and the manner of the drapes is that you take soft drapes, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye has need of; then strain it above a strong binding cloth, and repeat the poultices to suck up without causing harm; then remove the poultices and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the lien becomes worn out, then it is necessary that you restrain it much; then remove the lien after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good; if not, then repeat the plastering and draping and liening and poultices until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the bursting of the vitreous humor
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the vitreous humor, then it bursts forth, and comes out like a grain of resin, and it is so astonishing to see; then if you see it burst, the operation is such that you insert an awl into the root of the part below just up to the top, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the socket; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vitreous humor around, and strain it well, then remove the awl and put on the eye a damp linen cloth soaked in egg white; and let it be until the threads choose with the vitreous humor, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vitreous humor in each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes show great appearance, then puncture with a subtle spatula that comes from beneath the eyebrow, and correct the moisture albugina and descend the eyelids, and enter it in short order; then pull it out until it is clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bottom of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This malady which is called "alcunnati" is not outside the eye which is assembled in the pupil, appearing like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is that you sit the patient on a prepared and right siege, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the head so long as you see the bow come up to your eyes; then it should be fixed, and not descend and be dismantled, nor will the light diminish, and the patient will see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then place the patient's head between your hands, then take the subtle spatulum and make it go on the corneal tissue at the point of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, so long as the bow comes out; and when it is out, then distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey or boiling water mixed with fenugreek, then be cured by another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the tears of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have likenesses of waters in our division, and what is necessary for piercing; thus work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, outside of light for the sun, and keep the good eye and hold it very tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then put the point of the instrument next to the crown at the width of a bean on the edge of the eye towards the smaller tear duct; then push the instrument called "almagda" properly, and turn your hand until it pierces into the eye and feels that almagda comes into the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the length of the space which is from the prunella to the end of the nourishment; and that's the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper by the brightness of the corneal cloth, and then put the instrument just above or next to where the water is, then press it under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, then the patient sees it before him and the instrument is on his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little, and if the water rises again on the second path, put force with the instrument, and when it is stuck and will not rise, then extract slowly in circling your hand little by little; and then return to water some little gem, and leave off from that eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on top of the eye a poultice or a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, put on top a honeycomb with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", whose shape is:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep by far, but make it subtle, then put in alumina, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare the patient's bed with a dark cloth, so that he sleeps on his back in this tenebrous state; and be careful of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head or to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until three days later; then release him in the same dark room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage up to seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this during the cure or after the incision now, but rather hasten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Se apostemes chaus vient, that thou removest the eye in front of the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the aposteme; and when it is pacified, then remove the sight and place on its face a veil to cover for any day, and be there in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house step by step, and convert yourself to your place; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country he had seen someone make almagda pierce, which causes tears to flow, but I never saw anyone do this in our land, nor did I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see; and they are properly from iron.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these is made of this same subtlety, and the end in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	On the skin above
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are many times when diverse growths or sores appear, because of which there are some that seem like scorpions in many places; and if there are such ones, then the sore has been enchanted with flux of foul color, and the sore is soft of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then in that sore which is soft and not enchanted, it is necessary that you cause the patient to sit between your hands towards the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice onto those sores, and treat them fiercely; then grasp with what you can sustain at the fine edge of a razor on one side, as long as you know that that sore is completely dried.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be removed, then open it with all the subtle instruments gently, until nothing remains; and if without stirring or aposteme inflamed, then proceed as is necessary; and if it is malignant apostemes, then hasten and cauterize as much as possible, until the wound is stanchied and all the skins are removed; then pour in wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nail works and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is clean; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is flesh stuck in the bone above, which prevents instruments from coming: then you must put a piece of linen thread about a finger thick, and wet your hands with your fingers, and leave about an inch of space between each notch or less; and have the patient place the tip of the thread in their nail to some power, and pull it out gently as far as the inside of the mouth comes; and children do this many times at school, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes from the nail with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know the one after the other as you are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Treat that so long as you know that the night has corrupted that flesh, then take the son, stop the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back on the new skin just as before; do that for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put a bandage of cloth some days until he is healed, and if he needs drying medicines, use them; and that's the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicines on the new skin:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, semblant à une lampe ouverte, si comme une cainne, et li conduis ausi;
de la char sor le neis	On the skin above
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness called "telul" arises on the skin above the navel; it grows and becomes great in size until it is a visible thing to behold; and therefore it is necessary that you cut off the top, and remove all fat, then place the cautery or burning medicine upon it; and if one delays in cutting until it is great, take heed lest it become hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts into it at any time, a great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul color, and you see that you can cut it all off, then empty the patient and cut off the abscess without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knows that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
