Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to do thus with each one, if you look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together with a seam, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already split apart on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a seam, bind it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and incense upon powdered blood, and put a piece of strong plaster or another kind of plaster above, and let it sit for as long as it can by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses within the lips that are hard, resembling grains of millet, and smaller or larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each notch, and take out the contents with pincers and cauterize each part; then apply a poultice to the area after incision of vitriol bruised, until the blood is staunched; and then leave the lip open, and cure the area with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the skin of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth called "albulus" arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut off at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then place upon the area vitriol bruised, or other drying and desiccating powders; and if that growth returns after incision, and many times occurs, then cut it off again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; therefore it is necessary that you sit the patient in your hands, and his head be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness and jaundice and other discolorations, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at the first stage, it is good; but if not, then continue to repeat the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, for this reason that the rasor used to scrape away the teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing out as long as you can, for it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance just up to where one has no excuse for drawing.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to vomit, then it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth that is aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient suffers much pain and thinks it is the tooth of St. Peter, and has the good tooth pulled out; but the pain does not depart from him because of this, until the evil humor departs, for we have already tried to do so with those saints; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in all four spaces with a very sharp instrument to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your two hands or with subtle forceps at the first notch and notch, until it is well extracted, then secure the forceps well; and let the patient's head be in your holy place between your knees, and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and move it just as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	Et if the tooth is pierced and bitten, so it's necessary that you fill it with cloths, there where the perforations are; and if it's strained subtly with forceps, so it doesn't break when straining; and it's necessary to work carefully around the gum for dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient through the evil of the root causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like ignorant surgeons, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the carriage and bring about great diseases for the roots that remain or for the jawbone they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is torn out, wash the place with wine or vinegar and verjuice; and if blood comes, which often happens, apply the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles, so that they do not double back on you when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting, and should be made of well-forged iron, and should have teeth to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the roots stay at the rear, it is necessary that you put a wet cotton cloth on the place for one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the skin is softened, put in the forceps called "algefri", by which the head appears to be a gentle soother; and inside make them as if with a file, and that's the shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is also known as "palainche", of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is strong and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out by this means, that is good; but if not, then help it with all the instruments, of which the forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument that has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in proportion to the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like great tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters skilled in themselves find their instrument, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are some diseases where the ancient ones did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of bones and flesh, or it breaks on the bone or on another bone, or it can, then seek out the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and aid with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone, and it is small, then reduce all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural bodily form, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be soothed or trimmed: then file; and if it is rough with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the form, and it is similar to one small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp point above:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge is worn away little by little over a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can trim it, then use a file like this in its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little over a few days gradually, so that it does not move until it is even; then smooth out the end of all roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and hurt the tongue, then file off the roughness as much as needed, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front are loose, or by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without spitting, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but it doesn't work; then they must be restrained by a thread of gold, for silver wires become green and perish, but gold ones never do; and let the middle wire not be too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth aligning, take the thread and tie it double between two healthy teeth, then put the roots between the loose teeth, as many as there are one or more, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and gently, until it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the ends of the thread to a pair of tweezers, and assemble them, and rejoin between the healthy tooth and the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes undone or the threads break, so restrain it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its time, and that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, gradually and step by step, as we have said; and do not meddle with it if you are not wise and skilful, and at times make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and restrain it as we have said, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this ligament which comes below the tongue or naturally so, unless it occurs at birth or by accident of a wound that has been sewn up; and the work is such that you operate on the patient's mouth, with their head in your healthy one, and lift up their tongue; then tie off the nervous ligament from the wide part, until the tongue is freed from its place, and if there is hardness or night, it is due to a sudden wound, so put in the unguent and tie off that ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep near the artery which is below; and when you have done this, lift up the patient's head with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen tent under their tongue; and let the patient sleep every night so that the wounds do not sully.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Et if bleeding comes from decorum, then set it on the vitriol stone and broil; and if the blood flows freely, then cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that it is of foul color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards gangrene, and there is moisture, then apply an unguent, and cut a small opening with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the wound flows at your operation, then put vitriol powder on it until it is stopped, then return to your operation until you have done everything; then lift up the linen cloth and dry it, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a growth comes inside the throat called "godath", which are properly named II amandres; and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it is an abscess of little sense and a fusiform color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the bleeding of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is a white color around, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first look to see if the abscess has calmed down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sit the patient down before the sun, and his eyes should be in their socket, and let him open his mouth and grasp the instrument between his hands, and press his tongue below all the apparatus, so that is the shape; and it should be of silver or fine copper just like small knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue all over this instrument and see the abscess, then take a needle and thread it through the amber, and pull it tight above as much as you can; and leave nothing loose with the threads, then shape the instrument accordingly, so that it has the form that appears to be some force; and although the head is curved, and one end to another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or flint.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then shape it with pliers, so that it has the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make it taper from one end to the other; and when you have shaped one of the amber pieces, then shape the other in the same way; and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and if blood vessels appear, gargle the patient again; or use cooked apple pulp, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then continue to cure until they are healed; and sometimes new abscesses arise in the throat that are like the two amber pieces, so shape them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside the throat, to wit, a small sense abscess; and I had well closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and would have been dead if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had risen up more than two rows through the two openings of the birth canal.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hastened at once, and inserted an instrument into one opening, then the fire was lit, and a great portion of pus came out; then I refilled the other opening in the birth canal, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the instrument into this abscess, and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood issued; and thus the passage of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess would repeatedly grow back again, filling up the place I had emptied out, until it became very large; afterwards I bound it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left those parts, and let God do with them after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it rises up to the eye and is swollen and long, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a lump and rounded, then it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscess has calmed down, and it is subtle, then you should cut it; and the one that is rounded and assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a reddish color or black, then you should avoid making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we have remembered before this; then insert the onychine into the uve, and bring it out below, and cut at the two instruments that I said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover up the superfluity that is outside of natural bounds; for if you cover more, you will cause harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then it is necessary that you use artifice in the cauterization to eliminate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cauterization is with boiling water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter on cautery, and confesses with hot boiling water, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and in the use of this instrument, as is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient's head on a pillow or a cloth, just as hair is placed in a comb, and put the instrument on all of the medicine on the vein; and the patient should sit up straight on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, without going down to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand on all of the medicine and press it on the vein for the length of half an hour, until you see it turn white and the medicine's inflammation is appeased; and if you see anything, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the cane above, until the cotton reaches the vein; and do this many times until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start the medicine's cautery again, start it again, and afterwards apply a poultice around the vein with butter, and purify everything that surrounds the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and cured by gargling until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them into one pot, and add a little water, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with clay from a hard earth, and inside the pot have one instrument carved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or lead, and whether one of the keys is thrust into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is numbified; after which it often resumes, until the eye dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the warm swelling's advent, for many things happen then; and do not do this unless at the declination of the warm swelling.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cord and put a quill of egg inside the head, so that the patient's mouth does not have too much heat; for the quill of egg does not allow vapor to oppress the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it seems to be stuck in the throat like a bone or a fish spine, or something else; so it is necessary that you try what you can see and press the tongue on the sun with all the instrument, until you see the thing move; and whatever does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the top, it will be stuck, and then you will pull it out further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the top so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted high up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest all life depart from him, nor push the bone inside; and make sure the patient puts the instrument in place, because the thing is awkward; then push down, or pull it out fully with all the instrument equally, until it is fully out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the phlegm of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No time is medicine without sweat, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look at the patient's throat to the sun, then press his tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the abscess, so treat it with all small incisions, or with fine forceps that are worth for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth, take a braided cord, and put it in the throat of the patient, then bind the part of the cord with hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is troubled by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full vessel of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the abscess feels the water, it will burst.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not burst as we have said, subfumigate the patient with asafoetida, at the instrument that I have described in the fumigation of the ear; do this many times, for it will break without stirring.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has charcoal and viscera, and have a cloth covered with a perforated sheet in the middle, and in that hole put the key of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in their mouth and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out but comes just to the sweat; and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, then continue the fumigation many times; and let the patient thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for her to go forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the phlegm is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps for entering the throat; and it has a resemblance to a surgeon's beak, and on it there is an asperity of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and look at this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is the same as itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those wounds that are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the shoulder bone are different from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one must not pierce, until the pus is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their fulfillment, as are abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it be until it is rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay perforation until it is hard, so it will harm the main member; or if it is near the foundation, then one should pierce it as soon as it is dead; and it does not behoove that you pierce a hard abscess without digestion being accomplished, except for that which is near the foundation, lest it bursts forth and becomes elongated inside, and there comes to be a fistula; and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is soft according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and of the swelling and firming up of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where the abscess appears more dependent on its location, and where it opens outwards; and the perforation should be made from long to short in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, or arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who are afflicted, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in its early stage, so it is worth waiting that you leave the incision open until it is fully digested as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you make the incision before that, so the body of the abscess will become longer and filled with much pus, and by chance the lips and the depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be cut open according to the width of the body, as needed by the members.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small cuts, and in large abscesses, large cuts, and many splits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover and sew, when it has become as rough as a rag, and is exhausted, then you must do as one does with infants: and if there are those that are split in three angles, and if there are those from which you cut like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the armpits; and if there are those where you make a circular incision, and other cuts and similar suture.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not point of chief, if as aposteme soft superficial, it seems that you pierce plain; and it seems when the apostemes is big, and it has gathered great bowe, and you pierce, so do not pull out all the bowe in that hour, but a part; then stop the aposteme just until the next day, then pull out something else above; do this many times with ease, as long as the bowe runs out; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or women bearing, or little children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits jump out at times with the issue of the bowe, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then therefore eschew this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your aposteme, if the wound bleeds, and look to see if the wound of the aposteme is small; and if it's a plain cut, then stretch a tent of linen or old cotton over it; and if it's a large aposteme, and there are many holes, then it's necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come together one against another; and if you have cut into the aposteme some part of skin, and you have sewn it around, then it's necessary that you fill it with old cotton or flax cloth without moisture, and bind it to the third day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, then apply cold and easy water, and damp cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then apply a government and treatment, and the powders that I have said to be used in this book, and if it's during the winter, and the lesion or abscess is very nervous, then it's necessary that you put on wet cloths soaked in vinegar and hot oil; and if it's in summer, and the lesion is fatty, then it's necessary that you put on wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the abscess and the pus and treat it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how one should proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and see chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or when the head comes with small abscesses, and they are like the ways of us that are in meshes, just as the weaver of a spider's web, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It is of fat and such that has moisture also as pulps; and if there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the cut are such that you should try out all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then heat is applied above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape off without leaving anything on the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything; then plunge in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and silk, and apply the dressing to the wound, and let it be until the next day; and this cures what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, just as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that it will not remain overnight; then care for the wound with an ointment as is fitting, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not large, cut it according to this form, from long to short; and throw away the scabs, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in drawing out what lies beneath; and if the artery makes you contrary, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with the abscess if it is hard, and to cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut above the hard abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, for there will be less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or those that have no moisture are in the head or in an old woman; and I found one like a dull, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had done anything to it, they would have made as great a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, greater than those that come to the children's chief and the roots of the ears, let the opening always be at its most dependent place so that the pus may issue forth; and the cure should be done as it is needed.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are connected one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own place, just as the boil and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar cases of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Then, when you see a good disposition to touch it, and it is similar in color to the body, and quiet on all sides, and not hardening at the collarbone or artery or duct, and not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut above, and scrape off each part, and take out the two lips of the wound with your fingers, if you need to, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and proceed slowly and carefully, making sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor make a wound that is too wide or deep, so that your hand may escape, and do not go too far ahead, lest you do not cut what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put vitriol broth or some powders that stop blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work, until you have completed it; then examine carefully if there remain any small abscesses, and cut them and cleanse.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, then it is not necessary for you to cut that abscess at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall down without harm; then dress the wound with old Egyptian cotton dipped in oil.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire abscess, then it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no longer any superfluity remaining due to the greatness of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw forth, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, open there where it becomes clear; and the opening is done thus as was said before, depending on it, then introducing tentatives with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well purged, then the cure with ointment applies to the flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat, which is called "epiglote", be opened; and one does not make aid by this, because all the veins and the prominence of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the prominence of the neck, it is necessary to cut open the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the size of the syphac wound, not in the cartilage; and that place is suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the way around, then cuts the flesh as far as it comes to the chin; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the syringe, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the chin which bursts forth through the broken place and due to the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed about which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with care, and sew all together without leaving any cartilage; then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Also it says that one should not do this just yet until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and his life is slipping away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglote for this reason that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the womb; and I was summoned to heal her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and saw well that it had not yet been drained or led away from the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was well; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, and then returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in cutting into the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called an "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess with a greenish color, and it occurs mostly in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or the natural one has no fault.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is in two ways, which is similar to fat in us, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not necessary to make a fire except for what is small, and search all around: if you find it as I do not know how to treat fat, and cannot be healed by any means, then cut it out, just as one cuts out fat, and treat it with all its surroundings, if there is no pain; and search well everything, and cure it as needed, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of the tumor
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, which I will say all similar things; and now it is necessary that I say the whole difference that is between us and exit.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, until the suppuration has passed away, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nout there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a sac, which is its own pouch, and it is according to the color of the body, and begins like a small seed, and becomes large; and they are in two similarities, either fatty or moist, and much of their color are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the tumor, that you examine and investigate first all the instruments that are called "surrounding" tissues, according to what its form will be or chapter which comes later.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiry into abscesses in us is that you take or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two pokes and pokes until you know that the instruments have pierced the kernel, then as it is according to the greatness of the abscess; then extract the obstacle, and beware lest it burst forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture flows forth, regardless of its color, do it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes, know that it is fat, so do it then in a cross shape, and take hold with pincers, and scrape off lightly from each part and follow the direction where it lies, pulling it out whole without leaving anything behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is nothing left, it will come back many times; and if one piece remains and the blood troubles you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, apply pressure to the wound, and put on soothing poultices for hot abscesses, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure what remains.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another obstacle is contrary to your action, and you hasten and apply a poultice of vitriol, and let it lie two or three days or until the wound purrs, and the pus settles; then return to cutting off what remains of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here is the translation:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are many and similar, as you see here: great, medium-sized, and small; and also there are tumors that have two covers in three ways; and also there are tumors that have three covers, and they are the same in three ways; and also there are tumors that have two covers, and one cover only, and they are the same in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are cutting, and some have an edge that does not cut more than from one side, by which we skin the nose, because this is why we do not cut the vein or nerve; and among these intervening ones are the hemostats replied in straps, so that the patient does not feel anything at the opening of abscesses; and they are three kinds: great, small, and medium-sized, as you see; and one does not use more than one instrument in a charmed place, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument resembling skinning instruments, according to this form, by which we stem blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes at the place that heals completely from veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breast milk swells in certain men when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem breasts of a woman; and remain swollen and full, and whoever wants to cure them must shape them according to this form up to line .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and apply a medicinal poultice to the wound, releasing scabs; then bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast droops down and becomes enlarged like women's due to its size, as it does in women, so make an incision in two places above, through two similar fissures; from which one will be joined to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not yet fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, so you must fill the wound with damp cotton in corrosive oil; and leave it until the remaining fat and flesh are consumed, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard forms of scrofula or if it has nodules, and some of them contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment according to this form until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then cut it as we have said in incisions for scrofula, and if the wound yields pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
