When the artery is blocked and the skin above it is bound tight, so many times abscesses come; and likewise it happens to the vein being drained and abscessed; and if one knows this when it's because of the artery, then the abscess is long and deep inside; and when you feel it in your hands, then you feel a distance; and when it's because of the vein, then it appears as if it's gone away; and it's foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it's under the armpits and shoulders and neck and many other places, and it's very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to shun the fire treatment, and also he who is at the head should avoid it, and in him who has an inflamed artery going above the long skin; then make a cut on the pulse, and carefully uncover the artery from the ligatures, so that it is completely exposed; then insert beneath it an awl, and have it pierce through to the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you about the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then point the spot between the two ties with an injector so that the pus inside comes out and the abscess is relieved; then apply the treatment as before, until the ligature falls off; then treat those things belonging to ointment, according to what belongs to it, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of the vein, it is necessary that you take with your hand all that you can from the abscess to the entire skin, then insert the awl beneath the spot you hold in your hand, and have it pierce through, and there be a double thread, so that you draw it out on the other side; then bind the abscess as I have said, with the ligature of one of the two parts at the two joints of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads will not come forth, insert another awl throughout all the thread beneath all the abscess at the incision of the first awl, and restrain the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the superfluitous matters come out, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave what is bound; then apply a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, and then administer treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses in the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come to the artery and vein when they are ruptured or due to excessive strain, so too do abscesses come to the kidneys when they are fatigued or from excessive labor and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, and it happens more often at the joints and in all places where there are joints; and that's the grievous abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one is pressed firmly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not quite deep within the body, but just below the skin; and it will swell on all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and he who is at a joint does not need to be cut by iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and he who is in the head or in the forehead, will make the skin puffed out.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root; and if it is great, suspend it by the ligature, and scrape, then bone and sew the wound to the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great hanging lips
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Once upon a time it happens in bellies and not elsewhere thus the other place; and it is a disease that is called "fungi" by its resemblance to them and has fine roots and thick heads; and there are small and very great ones; and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else and there was no difference between them they were white and had fine roots and were split open and immediately began to corrupt with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6, and the operations of incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the abscess is white and moist and with fine roots; so cut at a spatula's width, and have the cauterization done by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess infected by enchantment, and I will come to the cure of abscess hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, and est sus le ventre and en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, or of sanc qui cort de voines or d'arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, or of ventositeit; and se c'est par la routure dou syfac and par l'issue dou bouel, si est li color de l'aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, and est legiere chose sens dolor, and apert de diverse issue.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers it springs back, and then returns, and by chance it may be solidified, and greatly swells at the entrance of the bath and through great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and apparent when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, so it appears by these signs the aposteme is great and hard, and fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windosity, so it is soft to touch, and the work is that you see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windosity.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or bowel, you must instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out straight, then signal all around the belly; then command him to lie down slowly between your hands, then move the site of the abscess around the belly, and cut off the top half of it at the great uncinate process; then tie it with a strong thread or cord securely, and have the surrounding tissue firmly bound; then work on the upper half of the abscess extended over the ligature, and inject your indicated dose, and cure the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, release it, and push the intestine back into the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, take it at the uncinate process, and remove the superfluity; and if the artery or vein resists, go slowly around, then return to your work and take two forceps, and insert two thin threads, and wrap the two forceps around what you have done in a cross as when you pierced; then strain the abscess into four places on the forceps, and if you see anything, remove the forceps, and leave the site so it can heal, and cut off dead flesh by yourself; or you will drain it when it becomes subtler and passable, then cure what is needed, and sever the abscess as we have said; and extract blood or moisture that you find, then cure the site of what is needed, and close the site.
dou chancre	of the abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the appearances of abscesses, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid iron treatment; and we say that abscesses are born in marshes, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients say that when abscesses are in a place or can be reached as if it were in the very flesh, and in the groin, and in similar places, one should remove it all at the beginning; and when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal from it, nor has anyone healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place or can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black bile at times; then make them healthy if they have manifest repletion; then prepare the patient a good place to do the work; then throw your gallows or abscess, and shape it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow out completely, and inspect the wound with your hand or some other thing; and if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it so that the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is done, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: thus it is revealed; and one should not touch with iron in these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and yposarche, for it is mortal; therefore when you treat this likeness of dropsy called "revealed" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another disease than dropsy, as all stomach troubles and similar things; so do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient with strong virtue, and they only have dropsy and are neither too old nor too young, then thus work: lift up the patient straight onto your hands, and the attendants press on the belly pushing out water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spatula-shaped bone according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cut at a point, and yet not so deep that it can come just to the intestine when you put it in, and cannot be injured; then look if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision of three fingers' breadth above on the point; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of three fingers' breadth; and if it is due to biliousness, make it on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that superfluities do not run to that weak part; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and stop it up, and lift your hand away from all the space between the skin and the fascia just as in shearing at the length of an eyebrow or around; then pierce the fascia until the spasm comes to its natural state, and that is the way of the water, then treat it further, and put this instrument back in which has the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it seems like a fine silver chain, and is of earth or light charcoal, and has three small holes in the part below; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut off like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instruments come to the water, they now flow down on the instrument; then empty half or a third part, for if you empty more than is needed at this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or they fall prone, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of their strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulse; then remove the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now because of the key that stops the hole which is on the syphilis, for which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and drain off a small quantity of water; do this some day, and take care not to flow until there is only a little water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient and leave much water, then cure of sepulture or warm sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and make him drink; and cure with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	None are born of children who do not have a wart on the penis, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is so necessary that he pierce at all the pores very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the wart in a clove of garlic, tie and hold it thus for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, then take out the clove, make him urinate, and then put it back; and by chance it does not need, because the urine that comes forth will not let the clove stay.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He who has a small perforation is treated with the remedy of blown glass, as we have said, so it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the perforation in its place are afflicted, for no one is born with the perforation at the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis high; and they cannot menstruate because the matter cannot reach the marriage bed, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient lies on their back, then place the head of the penis and cut it as one would shape a quill, so that the perforation opens in the middle, as it should; and be careful not to let blood flow from it which often happens, and if it does, stop it with something that stops bleeding, and cure the wound until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; and it is necessary that you take them at one time very subtly, and cut and clean all of them, then put a damp cotton swab in Egyptian oil; then treat with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of foul color and foul odor, then you must apply a cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it open, and if the boil is on the shaft of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is closed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you treat it together, so the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and there comes forth and corruption in its sheath and in the foreskin; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply the ointment made from the rind of green pomegranates and vinegar upon the powder of honey and flour, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, so apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterizes are of two dispositions together: that is to say, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, so it is necessary that you insert a linen thread into the urethra of the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair has grown out at the head of the penis which have not been circumcised, or there has been an injury or abscess, then it is necessary to cut it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and be delivered the head of the penis from all parts; and if this is a grievous thing to do, so it is necessary that you cut through the spatula some portion at the head of the penis and of the skin; then divide it carefully in two, and put a thin piece of moist linen cloth into cold water, so that it will not reattach.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the cutting off of continuity like other wounds; however, when we do this work by our own will and especially for children, it is necessary that we make the best possible work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have asked the greatest part of masters and saints who performed circumcision around one day, with great forces, and all a new moon; so it was the case where there are two skins, and by chance if you cut the top one and leave the bottom one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is to cut, and there is double pain, and the point of the member is not ensured; and at the mundification of the tongue by chance escapes the iron, and hinders the work, and many times it happens thus that they do not need mundification and I have asked.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mundification that is done with force, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you press your hand, cut it equally in all parts; but make sure the son is well wrapped around the skin; and the manner of the first work is this: cause the child to think that you are not doing anything more than tying the thread around the penis just once, and then let it lie in all ways you can; then let it rest between your hands straight up, and restore the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or blow, and draw it up as high as the head of the penis is; then clean it well from the filth that is assembled there, then tie the lead signet with a double thread, then tie it below one link to another link; and hold it between the two straps by the second strap on the pouch and at the ankle indicator, and cut between the two links, then lift the blowpipe above hastily and draw the head of the penis; then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for that is the mothers; and put powder on top and on top the powder sticks to a yolk of cooked egg mixed with rosewater, confited with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the mundification is this: the two fingers should be held and should be pressing, and should be equal in length.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the bleeding inside flows out at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the edges make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has subsided, and scrape lightly; then cut as much as you can move, and take care not to harm any part of the penis.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with sudden bleeding powder, which we have said or treated in the treatment of powders, and if you cut too much with the knife, and it goes above, then it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Li retenue of the urine is a blockage of stone, or blood congealed, or bladder, or new charcoal, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention due to the stone which is lodged at the back or nape of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and his feet should be placed on the back, and he should stretch his belly from above down to the back, and restrain himself as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder will be constrained to express itself through the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "siringue", whose form is this: and it should be made of fine silver hair, like the feathers of a bird; and it should be one and a half palms long, and it should be refined at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the top of a piece of wool or cotton, and put the top of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the surplus yarn and tie it just at the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a siege, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and dry water; then put the syringe lightly into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis above towards the mouth; then put the syringe forward just to the bladder, and let the patient feel come close to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conduit or way out is twisted; then let the thread be all along the wool piece and piece, and the urine will follow the yarn, then pull it out, and make the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or bleeding comes into the bladder, or putridity is assembled, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then make all the instrument called "clepsedre", and this is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	Elle est close, and if it has three holes: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the leaves are shaved so that the medicine is such that it stops well the urethra without addition, so that one can pull out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you put your medicines in the bladder, place the chief of the keusteur in the moisture, and draw on the drawing who is there; so you will draw the moisture to the keestour, and then push strongly on the drawing in; so the moistures will go in, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: thus.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of arnica, and the head is higher; and under one side or the cord falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see enemas the bladder, then tie between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pot on the fire; then insert the chief of the enema into the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture comes, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert the thread strongly in those holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles an awl, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and together with medicines and we have said the difference between the stone that is born in the reins and all the signs and in which stone one must work by cutting and in the bladder and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is born in the bladder is more common in children and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and then hair forms, and the patient's penis becomes hardened and inflamed, and it happens many times, and then it subsides; and many of these stones fall into the foundations; and childhood cures are much lighter until they have three years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is at its mean between youth and old age; and the cure is more light for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a cathartic, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it hinders sometimes from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift them up and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes come out high; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands be below his hips, so that the bladder is entirely declining downwards; then search and touch inside; if you feel the stone in place, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touching of all, moisten your two fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is weak, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger and insert it at the far end where you see it cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand above the coils, and with his left hand take away the skin that is below the coils in the part where you are making the cut; then put the spatula together, so it forms.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the left side of the naively; and be straight above the stone, and so be at the fundament, and be the width of the traverse if it is long in front, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too great; by chance the pressure may be so great that it jumps out without effort; and know that there are some stones which have angles and borders: it is difficult to emerge; and there are those which are smooth, like a glans, and rounded, through which the issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And then where there are angles and borders, make the width greater; and if it doesn't jump out, it is necessary that you stretch above with tongs that are like a file at the head, in order to strain the stone so it does not escape; or you place below the instrument, curved at the head; and if you cannot shape it thus, then enlarge the pore little by little, and if the sand falls out, strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, place first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then draw forth, and the small ones afterwards if there be more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be cut, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or urine flows freely where the wound cannot close; but still you should try with a file or pincers as tongs, until you cut it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense, aloes, and dragon's blood, and bind it tight, and apply a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil, rose water, and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then revive the patient by his neck, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, then arise very well the wound of oil and water, and then anoint him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses come to the wound and ulcers, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by these things, which is known in this way that urine does not flow with it: then pour your decoction into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and ruin it; then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help him in all ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works by which you cure him, that you bind his two buttocks together, and apply medicines to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra conduit of the penis, and stuck inside, and urine cannot come out; so take care as I say thus, that you cut many times, for cutting is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I already know it like this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and be fixed at three angles in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and wrap it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go further into the bladder; then push the bowstring into the penis lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the bowstring back and forth in the stone, as much as you can, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then urine will come out soon, and press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is soon broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders, then take one thread below the stone and another above, then bend the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and loosen the string, and clean up the congealed blood that is in the wound; and care for it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does happen, then the treatment is grievous, and it is defended against three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-known woman who will uncover herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, so it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder up to, until it comes to the root of the hip; then cut on the stone at the root of the hip against the middle of the crotch, there where it appears in its natural shape, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her thigh above or below the stone, and be the first small; then pour oil into the incision, if you sense the stone so far from the wound that the stone can come out freely, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with holes.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	So it is necessary to know the likenesses in order to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the bleeding abates, then put vitriol powder on the wound and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then come back to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones from men to help you with your work; and if the bleeding abates, and this is due to the artery that was cut, then put powder on the wound and strain of tents and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone alone, nor trouble it, lest by chance the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the place is clean, then return to your work until the stone is forth.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia of flesh
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramace aquouse is nothing else but the gathering of moisture or white leucorrhoea, which is below the skin of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "leucorrhoea", and sometimes it is properly in the web of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white leucorrhoea that we have said; and this does not happen unless there is nothing.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramace is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and it is spread out in that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And at times it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture takes many colors: or it's color declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or aquous white, and that happens often; and those are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is in white scab as we said, it is the abscess reopens, like a egg shape, and does not open the testicles, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, it is the abscess reopens with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white scab, one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, prove everything around the quartain, that is why the shape is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the surrounding quarter, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when we heal by fire, so it is necessary that the patient be cleansed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then have him sit on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths underneath him; then sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on the right, and extend the instrument to one of the sides of the kidneys; then take the spatula left, and cut the skin of the kidneys through the long part up to the point of the navel, and make the incision entirely straight while cutting the skin of the kidneys just so that it becomes white, and scrape subtilly according to our power; then pierce the white part plain with water in a large pit, and draw out all the water, and then put in onions, and stop the white part above; and do not touch the kidneys but only the white part; cut everything or by pieces similarly the edge of it subtil, that if you do not cut well, the water will return; and if the egg jumps forth to your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the syphac; then assemble the two leaves of the kidneys into a seam, then heal him as with other wounds, until he is sane.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie up the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the decoration of blood; then cut the testicle to all the suspended part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is gathered in two parts together, know that they are two roots; so cut the other part as you did the first one evenly, then stop the bleeding, and put in the wound a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil; and put another wet linen cloth soaked in wine and oil outside, and put above the two cones, and put above double cloths, and tie it all around with a cord according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and wrap them in wool according to this likeness and let them be sewn together in the belt of the braies, and one of the ends take above the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the fingernail; and the other end take above the two angles, and be all assembled with the rest of the binding in the buckle of the braier; and sometimes this root is treated with cauterization instead of iron surgery, and it's that you take a subtle cauterizing knife and cut the skin of the cones, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scab that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cauterizer according to this form, and pierce that scab into fine cuts, and scrape with this hot cauterizer.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And do the cauterizing in all ways that you can, until you have reached all; and take care that the fire does not touch the womb; and know that this work is more salutary; and beware of dismemberment of blood, and be mindful that the works of cutting are; and if nothing makes you contrary, whether it be aposteme or dismemberment of blood or other thing, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horror, then make a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs we have said that the abscess has subsided, then cause the patient to sit on a light siege; then pierce the abscess in the part below all the spatula's width, and insert the perforation into the length of the body; and let the holes be wide so that all the water can flow forth; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and let the remaining water run out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then you should insert a feather or the instrument with which one treats the waters of dropsy, by which the form is as before; and dilate the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or around that, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this reed-like thing there are many fears and preparations, for which it seems to me that more good comes from leaving it alone; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and indeed to the testicles; and this is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive bitterness and ague, which spreads to the groin or from percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a grievous abscess; and sometimes by chance a painful and hard abscess appears with a foul color, and sometimes comes from a burst artery, or an engorged vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to a burst artery, it is known by the hot abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it does not seem right for you to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from an engorged vein is known by its disposition to the expression of touching with fingers, and can well perform the cutting above this appearance, and on other sorts; and that you cut open the groin, then lift it up high, and treat the white sacrum, and deliver the suspending thing from all parts of the sacrum.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the blood is already saturated with these veins' contents, then it is necessary to draw out the blood and the copiousness; and if it is averse to the syphac, or in what is within the vessels, then it is necessary to release all that tenacity, and the copiousness again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the lump is in the back part, then it is necessary that you cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, and then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to that of the birchen bark, with the softening of the entrails, and the patient becomes grievously ill as he goes; and the cure for this disease is just as frightening as the previous one, and yet we will tell you how to do it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspensory of entrails down to your thighs, to all the vessels that are near the groin, and tie them tight; then cut into the spatula, cutting wide in the traversing place between the vessels, so that they are uncovered, and then scrape off each part, just as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in temples; then fix a needle where there is double thread, and tie it to the first position where the flesh has come, and tie it again to the other head; then cut into the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and drain off the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound just like the others or one that does not bleed, so that no vessel is left that nourishes one of the entrails; for by this, there will be no harm, and if all vessels come forth, it is necessary to drain the entrails to all vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and become dry and unable to help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the scab
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est by the section that comes out of the syphac, or the extension above the belly in the part of the groin, because the intestine descends from that rupture to one of the testicles; and this rupture is either from the syphac or from its extension, and there are these two ways it happens: either by percussion, or jumping, or brawling, or lifting a heavy load, and similar things; and when it's from the extension of the syphac, it has small drops, little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal down to the bottom, because the syphac presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the scab, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear in diverse forms, just below the skin, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's departure through the scab.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the umbilicus, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, wherefore one should avoid them with fear.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of working is that you instruct the patient to push the intestine into his hand as far as it will go in the wound; then have him look down at his navel. Then lift up his scrotum and stretch the skin above; next cut away all the skin from the testicles along their length. Then insert fingers of the size needed to open the wound, so that the bowels can emerge.
