If the wound is exposed to bone and is deep, and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of soft skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like pullets, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a purulent boil, and it is not at the bone, then cut out the boil entirely, and throw away the pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without delay, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it displaced, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put this powder which unites just as much as fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of living coal, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine as long as it is unhealed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coal alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but only if fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil has moved the wound, just as it is situated, then do not put on this powder; but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour and water with honey, until it runs clear; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between that and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the cure alone and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them recoil; and do not put cold things on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be careful with medicines, as if one were washing in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and then washing it again in sweet water, and other stones of similar kind, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, then bind it with cloth and tie with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	Et si les plaies sont parfondes et elle est chevee et pleine de boue, si la perce ou plus bas leu;
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife and the wound is deep, then see if there are symptoms of festering that cause the patient to redden: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it within the first hour nor bind it tightly for the blood that does not congeal in the depth, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but rather put attractive ointment on it, and bind it two times a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep on top of the wound for three days, or four, or more; then it will not come spasms, nor bad trembling from alarm; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then cure the wound and other cures, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and labor, then know that there is a fistula; so cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then cure what is in front of it; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is pressed into the bone, and there are broken pieces, then let the wound be, and treat the affected parts; and if they are not affected, then let the wound suppurate, so that the extractions will ease; and for other wounds on other limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruptions of the belly are great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes an intestine or the intestines will burst open, by which the introduction of pus occurs; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the great one, because one must put the intestines back in slowly, lest they go back in all at once; for when the intestines feel the cold, they swell and go back in slowly, and that is why the medium-sized wound is best, because one puts the intestine back in its place more easily. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners: two common sutures occur with the suture of the belly, and two other sutures proper for other wounds are also common; and although they are more suitable with the suture of the belly, I will say each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	When the wound is small and nothing from the intestines flows forth and there is no great issue to remedy, it can be done by one of two methods: or because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him thus: soak a sponge or cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook in hot water with cypress, spikenard, and squinny, and apply the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes make it reappear, and it will be sufficient to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with hot or lukewarm water, for it is constricted at the entrance to a small opening; and if nothing can enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used for bleeding; and the first cure is more important than the cutting, that no one should cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to use: if you cut within the curvature and do not cut too much, and see how it takes shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, so reset it to its natural form in its own proper place, if you are able, for this is a move.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, so you should make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then raise the head and breast higher than the parts below, and likewise if the injury of the belly is in one of the two parts, set your attention to what I say about great wounds and bandages.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Place what is on you, then take a pitous minister who holds all the wound in his hand and assemble the edges; and this is the common manner of stitching, that is to say, you take one or more needles, according to the quantity of the wound's largeness, then leave a space of two fingers' breadth from the wound's head, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two holes of the leather with the two holes of the siphac, which is below the leather inside, until you make it pierce on that part, and assemble the two ends of the siphac together; then strain one double thread around the needle for two parts, then assemble the two edges of the wound together, and then leave a space of two fingers' breadth, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to your need of needles, until all the wound is restrained; and be the needles moderate, between subtle and thick, for subtle needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot well enter: therefore it is necessary that they be moderate; and do not stick the needles too far into the flesh and leather, lest they pierce and open the wound before the suturing; then clip the needle's holes so they do not bother the patient at night, and put tents or cloths on the needle's holes to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is sutured; and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it suffices to use one or two; the second stitch is common, and is that you assemble the two leather edges and the two siphac edges together on a needle that has a moderate strong thread; and when you have pierced all these holes together, then remove the needle from the part where you began, as one sews cloth; and leave a space of the thickness of a smaller finger between each stitch; this stitch is known to men, and I stitched a wound that had been on a man's belly, which was wounded with a knife, and was more than a palm in size, and his intestines were two palms in size, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines when they had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was healed in just 15 days, and I cured it, and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the barber had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where we could not find any, nor any medicines; and I placed clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he became well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it through from outside to inside the part; when it has pierced the skin in straight lines, then place the head of the siphac or sewing thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce on the other side of the inside part to the outside; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew as the fuller makes fur, and leave once one end loose and take up the other, until the suturing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which Galen calls specifically, is such that certain people do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the chief ends of the silk to the other chief end, in this way: fix an awl or chief point of the mirror nearby, and make it pierce only that spot, and leave the two chiefs of the silk; then turn the awl, and make it pierce from the outer part just to the inner one, at the two chiefs of the silk; then make it pierce both of them from the outer part just to the inner one, in two other points of the mirror that are on the other side; and this is the more important manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify to it, so one must sew the belly with two awls, each having thread; and one should push one awl from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when there is a rupture within the belly, then the sewing is more difficult than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: and is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, then it is moved by fire, so put in the intestine, and the cloth; then put on powder inviting flesh, and if the fire has moved it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and trim the thread, and tighten the stitches, and the bandages; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to close, a piece of old cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many simple wound dispositions; and if you doubt that the wound will cause community to the main members, then it is necessary for you to moisten light linen in tempered heat oil or rose oil, and put it around the pangs, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or purulence in the bowels, and it often happens, then purge him with black wine vinegar, and likewise if the purulence comes just to the intestine; and poke inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the firmness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approaching nature of its kind to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the artery jumps out of the wound, put it back in place like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become white or black, then you must tie the part that is black, so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and let the two ends hang down from the part below the wound until the artery falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, because I saw a man wounded with a lance in his belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from there was coming the evacuation and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and the stitches were sewn.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this manner: take fresh figs, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the figs have opened the mouth, put them on the two lips so that his mouth stays open; and then cut off the head, and it will remain such that he cannot unfasten it; then put another fig after in this manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed; and dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That head if it is sewn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this thread from the intestine that is very clean, and then tie to the end of this thread another thin linen thread twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it through the route; and this manner of sewing with figs is not far removed from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it inflames, is universally called "fistula", and similarly when it breaks out and runs backwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the greenish nodation of faulty and white flesh, where one does not feel pain, and it bursts out like a bird's feather; and sometimes it runs clear and bright, and at other times thick and dense; sometimes little, and at other times sufficient; and I have spoken earlier in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed and there is no flesh left, is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, due to the weakness of blood or body; or due to its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to form; or there is too much discharge; or the limb is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or due to the property of the region being slow in digestion, and slow in healing, and flowing by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistula which is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula occurs in all members of the body; for it is fistulas that come to great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sacrum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so too does one come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are grievous to heal, and there is nothing but hard work, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come just up to what I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to recognize it, then take a tent of iron or clay, if the fistula is straight, then cut it; and if the fistula is bent, then search for a subtle tent of cloth, because the cloth will bend around the tortuousness; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well search it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the holes, because the moisture runs short from one hole to another, and purifies; then let blood as much as you know, whether there is bone or nerve, and is cut open in the middle, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand on him, and where it is; and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a jointure, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the false flesh and corrupted humors that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well purged from its right place, then cut open deep, as much as you can, then put moist tents in medicine, and pour them just up to the head of the fistula, so long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments in healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If vein or nerve does not grieve or principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so let it rest until all corruption is gone, then cure of things in the char will make it whole again; and if it is not whole, and returns to its former state, know that you are not yet at the end: uncover and seek until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus whole, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep in the bone, that you cannot approach it; if there is no other remedy than to rely on nature; and if there is a little corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pincers, then pull it out with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving none behind; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut and scrape and char, and deliver the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, so put on the wound a poultice allowing for purging, and leave until the pus is formed around the bones, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as that of the leg or hip, so restore only the corruption until all the mortification is gone, then treat the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted flesh, and comes to the very edge of the bone; so it must be cleansed and covered up to the corruption, and then cure until it is sound; and I will tell you about an abscess that happened to a man in his leg, so take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of thirty years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matters came to the leg and became swollen with a large abscess, and he did not have any reason to open it; but the doctors by their foolishness worked on it for so long that the abscess opened up, and much matter flowed out, and became a fistula, and there were many passages that all drained bowels and moisture from the body; and many doctors put treatment around two years, and there was no wisdom in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed out through the passages into great abundance; and the young man's body became red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I tented one of these hollows, and then searched all the hollows, and found that some came together on both sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and probed one of the hollows until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it to be rotten and perforated, and the rot extended right up to the bone inside; I saw what appeared from the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption except for what I had removed; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but couldn't heal it; then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the rot continued in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and thought of suturing the place; but I didn't get that far until I probed around one palm's width from the bone, and brought it all the way to its full length, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed quickly, and there was no need to continue the work except for the patient's weakness, which couldn't bear it, and due to my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation it often bled frequently, but it was whole and sound, and instead of bone there grew a hard skin, and it was in good condition and had no harm or contrariety from anything at all, neither to go nor come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be set in this way: take one strap and stretch it to the tip of the exposed bone; and have someone else hold it in place from above; and tie another strap made of coarse linen on top of the skin that is over the bone, and steady the tip so that you can pull out the rotten flesh below, and uncover the healthy skin above where you want to see; so that the setting does not damage the skin; and put a heated iron or a wooden splint under the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and it must be set as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and set again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in a middle or part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron underneath, and then reveal the corruption from one part to another, and be sure to take it as long as possible from the corruption I mentioned; and if the corruption is in the jointure, then cut the corrupted jointure, and be on the other side of the bone or its continuation; and if the corruption is at the finger tip of the hand or the foot, then it is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about this corrosion how it appears to you; and clean it up in all ways that you can, but let not the vein or nerve give you trouble; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, or by cause defuer; and when you have medicine that cures this corrosion by the treatment of medicines, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cover that member until the point where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes death, either from the mortality, which is greater, due to the default of the member; and the signs are such that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards pus comes forth, and then this corrosion spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; so hasten to cover, and if it is due to the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, and if the corruption is at the head of the foot, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut it off at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of his virtue; and thus do when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut the entire foot; and if it mounts to the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy except that the patient dies; and the manner of cutting or soaping the member is this: you bind it above and below, and stretch one servant down one cord and another servant up another cord, and you strip away the flesh which is between the two cords to a span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or soap, and put a cloth of linen on each side, so that the soap does not touch the healthy skin and brings another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, then cauterize the wound quickly, or put some restraining powders on top; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my care: he had a black ulcer that seemed like a fiery burn, and this corrosion came first on his foot, so much so that it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long after, the same corrosion occurred on the thumb of his hand, and he came to me, and I put some reflexive things on him after the purging of the body, but he could not stop the corrosion; and he thought that I should amputate his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repercuting the matter; and I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became desperate altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have told this story only because one makes another worse when one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Abscesses come to boil in a hard nut, and remain so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then they burst and perforate, and the pus jumps forth, and remains the hollowed-out nut, just as with vellum skins; and the skin above is as subtle as delicate drapes, and does not reach to the bone or the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain", and are not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone by the front, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is what you scrape off the skin all around, and similarly when it is subtle, just as with drapes; and it does not appear for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in the front, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat it with a clyster made thus: look if the breasts are large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then use the Egyptian medicine made thus: take equal parts of aloes, oil, and litharge, and mix them together in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and thick like honey; then take as much of this mixture as you need, and dissolve it in water and honey, and use it to purge the breast and close the fistula; let the medicine remain for two hours, then drain it by squeezing; do this many times until the breasts are cleansed and the pus is gone; sometimes one uses ash water when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from a vine trunk, pour water on top, let it flow, and use it to purge; as long as you know the breasts are well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure the medicine or the ash water, then use water and honey with a little litharge mixed in; or purify with honey and wine, for honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine makes the skin heal; and when you have done this, and you are confident that the breasts are well cleansed, then treat it with emplastrum definitivum, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in my treatment of ointments; and if the fistula on the breast is small, and the clyster cannot enter, so enlarge it a little with a ferret and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then cover it and leave only the opening of the clyster to enter, and if the fistula that pours pus is above, so cut or lower it down so that it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowels are in abundance, do not let them linger inside; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it in such a way that the bowels run to their lowest point which is; for when the bowels are abundant, do not let them linger inside and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it in such a manner: that the bowels flow gently downward and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidative medicines to place on the skin, and put a cloth of linen that covers the entire skin; then cut with force at the point where the breast is a little larger than before, and anoint softly on another cloth according to the size of the puncture, and place it on the puncture of the skin to lighten the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the puncture of the breast, often removes in order to remove the bowels, and know what flows from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in this manner and you see the nature that springs up on the puncture of the skin, know that the wounds are already healing, and approaching health; then free it in the morning, or the third day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the anointing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested bowel after many days, knows that the breast is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair at all about health, for the healings approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And there are people who put too much fat in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigestible bile jumps out of the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healthy; and if the breasts take long to heal and are swollen, then combine medicines with moist substance and dry virtue, as defined by ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the final medicine; take ointment defined, and mix it with rose oil, and equal amount of old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and do the same with honey boiled in growth, when ointment defined is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder on the honey when it is over fire; then glue I drapeling, and put it on the breast, and sometimes administer aristologe long, and roots of celestial lilies, which is like fine flour and centaurry; and use simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has entered deeply, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the joint
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a boil that grows under the finger web of the hand, or under the toe, or by chance occurs in other places; and when it is envellied, and one does not take care, so the boil bursts forth, and runs and flows down as long as it can reach the root of the boil, and by chance it reaches all the way; and comes to corrosion right up to the bone, until there comes a foul pain, and are the joints of the toe wide apart, and is the color fiery.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity that remains of the boil, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound, and the finger is healthy; and if the finger presses against the flesh, and begins to prick and bleed, then it is necessary that you put the rod underneath the pricking finger, and push it up, and cut away the pricked flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines in order to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et if the decay is in the bone, so hack it out, and trim away, for as long as the bone is decaying there, it cannot heal; and if you see the joint decaying, so cut into it at the point where we said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is infected, and swollen, and it feels great pain, so be sure to heal it first; then cut out the ulcers of the spatula's knife by cutting across above, and take care that the cutting does not come all the way to the flesh which is beneath the ulcers, for the patient would feel too great a pain; and if there is, place something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is sometimes a bone or it has a bone, and sometimes there is an ulna, and one of them is born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cil who is born in any notch of the elbow does not move, and he who is born at the jointure of the elbow by chance moves; the stature of one who is fat so is light, in this manner: his stature is in its root like a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: if you take it to be cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or should be at the rear notch, it is necessary that you scrape off the flesh to just below the bone, then scrape the bone with a suitable thread for that, then heal it until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come together come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you scrape off the weld, and then repair it according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or wet cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you can put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the limb is healed, just as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cover that swelling as it should be.
des vils	of evil things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Venous veins are large and swollen, full of superfluous melancholic fluids, which come to more members of the body; and it happens most in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him occasional purging with vinegar, and then heal with the oil of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron treatment is according to two manners: one is when you scrape and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The surgery is done in this manner: first, arise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned, then restrain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then lift and draw out the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood issues as the virtues of the patient can endure; and then tie it up, and command that they eat nourishing foods allowing black stool; and recommence evacuation and purging when the veins are full, and is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: Raise the patient's leg if it has many hairs, then put it in water and let it soak until the veins swell; and if you don't have water, warm it by the fire and then cut into the vein at the long part of the thigh or below the knee; then scrape away the skin around each vein until it feels like a taut string; and see that it is red and black, and when it goes into the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the thread underneath, so that it rises out of the skin, and then gently pull it to the next thread; and cut another length, or as many times as you need, then lift it and cut again at the ankle bone; then drag and lift just up to the second length; then draw it from length to length until it is all loose, then cut; and if you cannot draw and lift, put a needle on all strong double thread, and lift and draw, and put underneath the thread, and turn your hand this way and that, so long as it comes out; and take care not to cut, because if it cuts, one cannot draw or lift, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put a damp cloth on top of the wound in wine and olive oil ointment; and cure until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and looped together, and it's not straight, as we have said, so you must cut it obliquely, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one coppers the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it opens up the vein; and is a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes from beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms arise between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this flux are that a very great inflammation comes to the leg, then the swelling changes shape and the flux begins to issue forth, just as a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling opens up, it's necessary that you wrap a piece of cloth around one and a half to two times, and tie it off, leaving the cloth on the leg, and every time it goes away from the front, you wrap it again around the cloth, and tie it off; and if it's too long, you cut off part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and don't cut it at its root until it's completely gone; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about abscesses and putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease; therefore it's necessary that it be treated gradually up to the top, and none remains in the body; and sometimes this flux is when it's treated from five or ten fingers long, or even one man came to me who had it come out of ten finger-lengths long, and when you cut it, you push a reed or a pike through, and it goes all the way down until everything comes out; and then the material inside is emptied, and medicines are administered to prevent putrefaction some day, and then the cure takes place just as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at this point many streams flow, and indeed especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or the foot itself, and a great deal of pus comes out, and then there are many streams; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "beef sickness", because it often attacks oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one feels it well from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and then bursts; and it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, serpents, warts, and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye, it may happen that it enters and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and moving, one can't help but wait until it goes: so it is necessary that you bind the area above and below with a strong cord tightly, then strike up and pull it through, and if the pus is poured deeply into the flesh, and you don't find it, then cauterize it with fire above, until it dries; and the greatest harm it causes, it is that it flows to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, so bind below it a bandage tightly, then strike up, and pull it through; and it is necessary to use the patient of purifying medicine solutions for bad humors, and be wary of foods that cause putridity.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
